 HDUS TREASURY OUTLOOK-Data to stir market before Fed decision      BYBy Ellen Freilich      WC607 words   PD30 October 2007   ET21:06   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LPNEW YORK, Oct 30 (Reuters) - A number of important economic reports could impact U.S. government securities prices on Wednesday as investors wait for the Federal Reserve to make its afternoon interest-rate announcement.   

Financial markets largely expect the Fed to cut benchmark rates by 25 basis points on Wednesday, a follow-up to the U.S. central bank's 50-basis-point rate cut in September.   
   TD"Monetary policy works with a lag of six to nine months and almost everyone is forecasting a really sluggish, weak economy for the first half of next year," said Bill Hampel, chief economist for the Credit Union National Association, predicting that the Fed would cut its federal funds rate by 25 basis points to bolster "a below-trend, borderline recession economy in the first half of 2008."   

But before that afternoon announcement, about which there is still some suspense, the market will get a number of substantive economic reports that could stir Treasury prices even as investors wait to hear from the Fed.   

Some analysts said the imminent rate announcement could constrain the market's reactions to these reports.   

Others said reaction to the fresh economic data could be somewhat magnified by the realization that the Fed will be incorporating these latest data -- including third-quarter GDP, inflation and employment costs, September construction spending and October regional manufacturing -- into its rate decision.   

"These may be the final inputs into the Fed's ultimate decision on interest rates and given that they will be closely scrutinized, they could impact the tempo of trading going into the Fed's decision in the afternoon," said William Sullivan, chief economist at JVB Financial Group in Boca Raton, Florida.   

Among the most closely watched economic data on Wednesday before the Fed's rate announcement will be the government's first estimate of third-quarter gross domestic product growth, expected to show GDP grew an annualized 3 percent last quarter, with core personal consumption expenditure prices, the Fed's favored inflation gauge, rising at a 1.5 percent rate, safely in the Fed's presumed "comfort zone" of 1 to 2 percent.   

The October Chicago PMI -- expected to read 53.0, down from 54.2 in September -- will be watched for hints about the state of manufacturing at the start of the fourth quarter and to get a sense of what the nationwide ISM manufacturing index might look like when it is released on Thursday.   

The ADP employment report on private sector employment growth in October will get attention as traders try to get a better fix on what the Labor Department's monthly employment data will reveal when it is released on Friday.   

September construction spending, due at 10 a.m. (1400 GMT), the same time as the Chicago purchasing managers report, is estimated to have fallen 0.5 percent after a 0.2 percent increase in August.   

The Treasury's quarterly refunding announcement, scheduled for 9 a.m. (1300 GMT), is expected to be a 'nonevent' with so much economic data being released and the Fed about to make an interest-rate announcement, analysts said.   

"Trading could be a little more volatile on Wednesday (than it would normally be on the day of a Fed rate decision), but reactions to economic reports will be quick," said John Canavan, analyst at Stone and McCarthy Research Associates in Princeton, New Jersey. "Then it will settle in again until the Fed announcement. It will be tough to find much momentum."   
   RFMARKETS-BONDS-OUTLOOK|LANGEN|ABN|M|D|E|RBN|U|MNI   NSe1122 : Mortgage Applications/Refinancing | e1202 : Interest Rates | m131 : Money Markets | mgvdbt : Government Debt/Bond Markets | e11 : Economic Performance/Indicators | e12 : Economic/Monetary Policy | ecat : Economic News | m12 : Debt/Bond Markets | m13 : Money/Forex Markets | mcat : Commodity/Financial Market News | ncat : Content Types | nfact : Factiva Filters | nfce : FC&E Exclusion Filter   REusa : United States | namz : North America   IPCMMT | DBT | GVD | AGN | MTG | STIR | MCE | MUNI | US/O | EMBG:DBT | embargokeyE1   PUBReuters Limited   ANDocument LBA0000020071102e3au002a3  



 HDHong Kong lowers  interest rate  quarter point in wake of US  Federal Reserve 's cut      WC475 words   PD1 November 2007   ET11:26   SNAssociated Press Newswires   SCAPRS   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007.  The Associated Press.  All Rights Reserved.   
   LPHONG KONG (AP) - The Hong Kong Monetary Authority -- the Chinese territory's de facto central bank -- cut its base lending rate to 6 percent from 6.25 percent on Thursday after the U.S. Federal Reserve's quarter-point cut overnight.   

Banks in Hong Kong quickly followed by announcing cuts themselves, offering some relief to borrowers but dealing a blow to savers.   
   TDBank of China Hong Kong,  Hong Kong & Shanghai Banking Corp. and Hang Seng bank all said they would lower their prime lending rates to 7.25 percent from 7.50 percent, effective Friday. Standard Chartered cut its prime rate to 7.50 percent from 7.75.   

The HKMA's move was widely expected as the former British territory's monetary policy tracks closely that of the U.S. because of its 24-year-old peg to the U.S. dollar.   

The monetary authority has pledged to keep its base rate -- the reference rate for the lending of overnight funds to local banks through its discount window -- fixed at least 1.5 percentage points above the federal funds rate.   

The Fed on Wednesday cut its target for the federal funds rate to 4.5 percent from 4.75 percent. It last cut rates in September, a move that the HKMA also matched.   

Banks in Hong Kong are not required to follow the monetary authority's move, but usually do. Earlier this week, some banks had suggested they may not match the rate cut because of a high interbank rate -- the rate at which banks lend money to one another.   

Driving up the interbank rate has been an insatiable demand for Hong Kong dollars. Foreign and local funds are buying into Hong Kong's red-hot stock market in anticipation that Beijing will soon allow mainland Chinese to invest in Hong Kong.   

The demand has also pushed up the strength of the local currency, prompting the Hong Kong Monetary Authority to step in and buy U.S. dollars in a bid to keep the Hong Kong dollar within its narrow trading band.   

On Wednesday, the authority intervened five times, selling a total of HK$7.828 billion (US$1 billion; 690 million) to defend the local currency's peg to the U.S. dollar.   

HKMA Chief Executive Joseph Yam said the local dollar's strength against the greenback was partly driven by speculation, but the city's government was committed to maintaining the peg.   

"The linked exchange rate system has been functioning well to deliver exchange-rate stability," Yam said Thursday in his weekly column on the HKMA Web site.   

"There is no plan or intention to change the system in any way (such as re-pegging at a different level or widening" the trading band, he said.

 HDEnergy, metals and agricultural futures fall ahead of  Federal Reserve interest rate  decision      BYBy LAUREN VILLAGRAN      CRAP Business Writer   WC647 words   PD30 October 2007   ET20:31   SNAssociated Press Newswires   SCAPRS   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007.  The Associated Press.  All Rights Reserved.   
   LPNEW YORK (AP) - Commodities prices declined Tuesday as uncertainty about the Federal Reserve's upcoming decision on current interest rates and future policy left investors jittery.   

Oil prices retreated sharply from a record just shy of $94 a barrel on Monday, while gold, silver and industrial metals prices declined. Agricultural futures also fell back.   
   TDThe Fed's decision about key interest rates, and any indication it gives about the direction of monetary policy, has bearing on the strength of the U.S. dollar and, indirectly, on commodities prices. A rate cut -- which investors widely expect -- could further undermine the greenback, boosting commodities prices by drawing more investors into the markets for energy and metals as a hedge against the currency's decline.   

The central bank's move is expected at the conclusion of its two-day meeting on Wednesday.   

Although a poorly performing housing market, strained credit conditions and sluggishness in other areas of the economy have bolstered the case for lower interest rates, record oil prices and high raw materials costs have sparked concerns about inflation -- which could hold the Fed back from a rate cut.   

Investors are also waiting for Wednesday's initial estimate of third-quarter GDP and construction spending for September, both reports due from the Commerce Department.   

Crude oil tumbled $3.15 to settle at $90.13 a barrel on the New York Mercantile Exchange. Gold dipped $4.80 to settle at $787.80 an ounce on the Nymex, while silver shed 10.2 cents to $14.328 an ounce.   

November gasoline futures fell 7.03 cents to settle at $2.2571 a gallon, and November heating oil slid 4 cents to settle at $2.4246 a gallon.   

The dollar gave up ground to the euro and traded mixed against other major currencies on Tuesday; it's fallen more than 9 percent against the euro this year alone.   

Dollar bears may be getting nervous ahead of the Fed decision on interest rates, said  MF Global analyst Edward Meir, in a report. Should a cut be paired with a tougher policy statement, the dollar could jump. If the markets get no rate cut at all, that "would be a severe jolt to all the markets, and result in heavy dollar buying, which inevitably would pressure commodities even further," he wrote.   

Rising stockpiles of base metals held by the London Metal Exchange, and uncertainty about interest rates, combined to pressure prices of copper, aluminum, zinc and other metals.   

More bad housing news also hurt the metals market. The S&P/Case-Shiller index on Tuesday showed U.S. home prices slid for the eighth straight month in August. An index of prices in 10 metropolitan areas declined 5 percent in August from a year ago, the biggest drop since 1991.   

On the Nymex, copper for December delivery slipped 3.95 cents to close at $3.4815 a pound.   

Energy prices mostly weakened ahead of the Energy Information Administration's report on petroleum inventories, due Wednesday. Analysts polled by Dow Jones Newswires forecast a modest increase in crude oil inventories of 100,000 barrels, on average, and declines of both gasoline and distillates. However, last week's report took the market by surprise with a huge, 5.3 million-barrel draw on crude stockpiles, propelling oil prices over $90 a barrel.   

Gasoline for November delivery fell 7.03 cents to settle at $2.2571 a gallon, while heating oil dipped 4 cents to $2.4246 a bushel.   

Agricultural futures declined on the Chicago Board of Trade. December wheat dropped 14.5 cents to settle at $8.14 a bushel. December corn fell 5.75 cents to $3.7025 a bushel, while soybeans for January delivery fell 19.5 cents to $10.0925 a bushel.   
   RF5   INi13 : Crude Oil/Natural Gas | i1 : Energy   NSm14 : Commodity Markets | m143 : Energy Markets | m15 : Derivative Securities | mcat : Commodity/Financial Market News | mcroil : Crude Oil Markets | e1202 : Interest Rates | e12 : Economic/Monetary Policy | ecat : Economic News | ncat : Content Types | nfact : Factiva Filters | nfce : FC&E Exclusion Filter   REusa : United States | namz : North America   IPCtagapf | selapfin | catf   IPDFinancial/Business | APFN Commodities Review | D8SJOE8G0   PUBPress Association, Inc.   ANDocument APRS000020071030e3au003uk  



 HDFed Pumps $41B Into US Financial System      BYBy JEANNINE AVERSA      CRAP Economics Writer   WC364 words   PD1 November 2007   ET22:15   SNAssociated Press Newswires   SCAPRS   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007.  The Associated Press.  All Rights Reserved.   
   LPWASHINGTON (AP) - The Federal Reserve pumped $41 billion into the U.S. financial system Thursday, the largest cash infusion since September 2001, to help companies get through a credit crunch.   

The action came one day after Fed Chairman Ben Bernanke and all but one of his central bank colleagues voted to slice a key interest rate. It was the second time in six weeks that policymakers acted to protect the economy from the effects of the housing downturn and credit troubles.   
   TDWall Street took a nosedive with the Dow Jones industrials losing 362.14 points to close at 13,567.87.   

The Fed on Wednesday ordered its key rate, called the federal funds rate, to be lowered by one-quarter of a percentage point to 4.5 percent. That followed up on a half-percentage point cut in September. Those two rate reductions might be sufficient to help the economy make its way safely through trouble spots, Fed policymakers indicated.   

The funds rate affects many other interest rates charged to millions of individuals and businesses and is the Fed's most potent tool for influencing economic activity.   

The  Federal Reserve Bank of New York, which carries out the central bank's open market operations, moved Thursday to inject $41 billion in temporary reserves into the financial system.   

A New York Fed spokesman said it was the largest single day of operations since $50.35 billion was pumped into the system on Sept. 19, 2001, following the terrorist attacks on New York and Washington. He declined further comment.   

Fed policymakers at their meeting on Wednesday noted that the "strains from financial markets have eased somewhat on balance." In the past week, many Fed officials have described the state of financial markets as fragile.   

Bernanke and other Fed officials have said it will take time for the markets to fully recover from the credit crisis.   

Since August, the Fed has been pumping cash into the financial system to help ease strains from the credit crunch. It also has cut its lending rate to banks -- a third such cut came on Wednesday.

 HDAustralian dollar hits 23-year high against US dollar      WC118 words   PD1 November 2007   ET00:45   SNAssociated Press Newswires   SCAPRS   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007.  The Associated Press.  All Rights Reserved.   
   LPSYDNEY, Australia (AP) - The Australian dollar hit a 23-year high against the U.S. dollar Thursday after the Federal Reserve lowered a key interest rate by a quarter percentage point to 4.5 percent.   

The Australian dollar opened trade at US$0.9312, its highest rate since April 4, 1984. Analysts expect the currency could top US$0.94 if the Reserve Bank of Australia lifts interest rates next week.   
   TDEconomists have widely predicted the central bank will lift a key interest rate by a quarter of a percentage point to 6.75 percent to contain inflationary pressures in the economy.   

The announcement is expected Nov. 7.

 HDGrocer shares drop on fears that Fed will end its rate cuts, slowing economy      WC227 words   PD1 November 2007   ET21:08   SNAssociated Press Newswires   SCAPRS   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007.  The Associated Press.  All Rights Reserved.   
   LPNEW YORK (AP) - Grocer shares dropped Thursday, led by a big decline in  Winn-Dixie Stores Inc., as investors feared an end to interest rate cuts amid a slowing economy.   

Stocks across the market dropped as the price of oil passed $96 per barrel for the first time overnight and a Commerce Department report indicated consumers didn't spend as much in September.   
   TDResponding to the slow economy, the Federal Reserve cut a key interest rate by a quarter point Wednesday. But the Fed also said that inflation remained a concern, signaling that it was unlikely to cut rates again.   

Winn-Dixie shares fell the hardest in the grocer sector even though the company reported a narrower first-quarter loss earlier in the week.   

Here is how some key grocer stocks did Thursday:   

Kroger Co. fell $1.19, or 4.1 percent, to $28.20.   

Safeway Inc. lost $1.13, 3.3 percent, to $32.87.   

Great Atlantic & Pacific Tea Co. Inc. declined $1.41, or 4.4 percent, to $30.96.   

Supervalu Inc. eased $1.19, or 3.1 percent, to $37.56.   

Winn-Dixie Stores Inc. tumbled $3.54, or 15 percent, to $20.10.   

Whole Foods Market Inc. retreated $2.33, or 4.7 percent, to $47.21.

 HDUS Fed cuts key  interest rate  for a second time to guard against recession threats      BYBy MARTIN CRUTSINGER      CRAP Economics Writer   WC880 words   PD31 October 2007   ET20:45   SNAssociated Press Newswires   SCAPRS   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007.  The Associated Press.  All Rights Reserved.   
   LPWASHINGTON (AP) - The Federal Reserve, confronted by surging oil prices and a slumping housing market, cut a key interest rate by one-quarter of a percentage point Wednesday. But policymakers signaled that may be all the rate relief the U.S. economy needs right now.   

The central bank lowered the federal funds rate to 4.5 percent, as expected. While financial markets had hoped for a clear sign of further cuts, the central bank indicated that rates cuts in September and October may be enough to stave off the threats of a recession.   
   TDEconomists worry that growth will slow dramatically over the final three months of the year because of the housing slump, a credit crisis and record-high oil prices. The Fed, however, sounded a more upbeat tone.   

The Fed also cited continued worries about inflation and said it believed that after the two rate cuts, the risks between weak growth and higher inflation were roughly balanced.   

"The odds of another rate cut at the December meeting are substantially less than they were before this statement," said David Jones, chief economist at DMJ Advisors in Denver. Jones said he still expected one more rate cut to deal with a weak economy, but it probably would come at the Fed's January meeting.   

Commercial banks responded to the Fed's decision by announcing a quarter-point cut to 7.5 percent in their prime lending rate, the benchmark rate for millions of consumer and business loans.   

Wall Street sagged a bit immediately after the announcement, but quickly regained its footing and rose by more than 100 points in late afternoon trading.   

In a brief statement explaining its decision, Fed Chairman Ben Bernanke and his colleagues said they now judge that "the upside risks to inflation roughly balance the downside risks to growth."   

Stating that risks are now almost balanced was seen as a signal that the Fed believes further rate cuts may not be necessary.   

The Fed's decision came on a 9-1 vote. Thomas Hoenig, president of the Kansas City regional Fed bank, dissented and preferred no change.   

The Fed had lowered the funds rate by one-half of a percentage point at its Sept. 18 meeting.   

Commenting on the economy, the Fed was more positive than last month, when it expressed concerns about the toll the credit crisis would take on housing and the overall economy.   

"Economic growth was solid in the third quarter and strains in financial markets have eased somewhat on balance," according to the Fed statement.   

The central bank said the pace of the economic expansion "will likely slow in the near term, partly reflecting the intensification of the housing correction."   

The Fed met on the same day the government announced that the overall economy grew at a stronger-than-expected 3.9 percent rate from July through September.   

Many economists believe growth will dip to around 2 percent from October through December and may slow even further, to about 1 percent, in the first three months of 2008.   

The Fed said the reading on core inflation, which excludes energy and food, had "improved modestly this year." But the central bank worried about what the recent increases in energy prices and other commodities might do to inflationary pressures.   

The committee said "some inflation risks remain," a signal it will be hesitant to cut rates further because of concerns on inflation.   

The Fed had pushed the federal funds rate up a record 17 consecutive times in quarter-point moves over two years. The last increase was in June 2006.   

From that time until last month, the rate did not change. The Fed watched to see whether its credit tightening had the desired effect of slowing the economy enough to lessen inflationary pressures.   

But the worst housing downturn in more than two decades has threatened the Fed's goal of slowing growth and containing inflation.   

Economists worry that the credit crisis this summer will make home sales and prices fall even more, undermining consumer confidence and causing consumers to cut back on spending.   

Bernanke, who took over as Fed chairman in February 2006 from Alan Greenspan, came under criticism in August when the Fed left rates unchanged and said inflation was the primary economic threat.   

But two days after that meeting, when a severe credit crunch hit world financial markets, the Fed provided billions of dollars in cash to the U.S. financial system and cut the rate at which it makes direct loans to banks. Then, on Sept. 18, the Fed reduced the funds rate by one-half of a percentage point, which was more than expected.   

Lyle Gramley, a former Fed board member and now an economist with  Stanford Financial Group, put the chances of a recession at around 40 percent. He said the Fed's primary concern is what is happening in housing and how much of a spillover that will have on the overall economy.   

"It is possible that the housing industry will take us over the edge into a recession," he said. Gramley noted that every housing downturn of the past 60 years, except for two, have triggered recessions.

 HDWall Street plunges on fears that  interest rate  cuts will end even as economy is weakening      BYBy JOE BEL BRUNO      CRAP Business Writer   WC1,013 words   PD1 November 2007   ET22:44   SNAssociated Press Newswires   SCAPRS   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007.  The Associated Press.  All Rights Reserved.   
   LPNEW YORK (AP) - Wall Street plunged Thursday, pulling the Dow Jones industrial average down more than 360 points as investors found themselves confronted by two uncomfortable prospects: an end to interest rate cuts and a slowing economy.   

Mindful of a warning from the Federal Reserve Wednesday about inflation, the market nervously watched the price of oil, which passed $96 a barrel overnight for the first time before dipping on profit-taking. The Fed, which cut interest rates a quarter point, said in a statement that inflation remained a concern, and oil's ascent to another record raised the possibility not only that the Fed might stop cutting rates, but that it might even consider raising them if inflation accelerates.   
   TDMeanwhile, Wall Street also had to contend with concerns about a slowing economy. A report from the Commerce Department indicated consumers scaled back their spending in September as worries mounted about a worsening housing market and further credit market turmoil. And a trade group reported that manufacturing in the U.S. grew in October at the weakest pace since March.   

The combination of factors led investors to pull back sharply from Wednesday's rally, in which the Dow climbed 137 points after the Fed said the economy had weathered the summer's credit crisis.   

"Wall Street is in love with the idea of a rate cut, and realized that the Fed said inflation is still a concern -- that lowered the chances of a cut in December," said Ryan Detrick, a senior technical strategist with Schaeffer's Investment Research. "We're now feeling the pain now that investors have slept on it, and figured out what they said."   

Christopher Cordaro, chief investment officer at RegentAtlantic Capital, said Wall Street remains anxious about the possibility of recession. He also believes the market is devoid of enough positive news "to have any type of sustained rally."   

Investors were unswayed when the Fed pumped $41 billion into the U.S. financial system, one of its largest cash infusions since the credit crisis began in the summer. This increases the amount of money banks have to lend, and helps improve liquidity. In the past, such an action helped soothe the market, but that was not the case Thursday.   

With the market growing pessimistic about the economy, the Labor Department's report on October jobs creation, scheduled to be released Friday morning, will be taking on even more importance than it usually has. The data is expected to show unemployment remained steady in October, with payroll growth of 85,000 new jobs, compared with 110,000 in September.   

The Dow fell 362.14, or 2.60 percent, to 13,567.87.   

The Standard & Poor's 500 index was off 40.94, or 2.64 percent, at 1,508.44, while the Nasdaq composite index dropped 64.29, or 2.25 percent, to 2,794.83.   

Big late-session moves became common on Wall Street during the summer. Investors remain hopeful that a down market will turn around, but tend to launch a late afternoon selloff if that doesn't happen.   

"We've been getting all these mixed signals, and this is just a confluence of bad news between the Fed, the financials, and this mixed earnings season," said Chris Johnson, president of Johnson Research Group.   

Financial stocks were pummeled after  Citigroup Inc. and  Bank of America Corp., the two biggest U.S. banks, were downgraded by CIBC World Markets on worries about the credit markets.   

Investors pulling money out of stocks turned to the safe haven of the Treasury market. The yield on the 10-year Treasury note dropped to 4.35 percent from 4.47 percent late Wednesday, and was unchanged in after-hours trading.   

Crude prices vaulted above $96 per barrel in overnight trading. A barrel of light sweet crude settled down $1.04 at $93.49 on the New York Mercantile Exchange.   

The Commerce Department's report that consumer spending rose by 0.3 percent in September, slightly lower than the 0.4 percent increase that analysts expected, raised concerns about a slowing economy.   

In addition, the performance of the manufacturing sector in October suggested that ongoing troubles in the housing and credit markets have seeped into the industrial sector. The Institute for Supply Management, a Tempe, Ariz.-based trade group, reported its manufacturing index registered 50.9, down from 52.0 in September and below expectations for 51.8. A reading above 50 indicates growth; below that spells contraction.   

Also Thursday, the Labor Department said the number of people filing for unemployment benefits declined by a larger-than-expected 6,000 last week to total 327,000.   

Wall Street was also troubled by the day's corporate news.  Exxon Mobil Corp., the world's largest publicly traded oil company, reported third-quarter profit fell 10 percent because of lower refining and chemical margins. Shares of the Dow component dropped $3.49, or 3.8 percent to $88.50.   

Bank of America, the No. 2 U.S. bank, dropped $2.57, or 5.3 percent, to $45.71. Citi, the nation's largest financial institution, dropped $2.85, or 6.9 percent to $38.51 -- its lowest level in four years.   

Declining issues outnumbered advancers by about 4 to 1 on the New York Stock Exchange, where consolidated volume came to 4.20 billion shares, compared to 3.84 billion shares on Wednesday.   

The Russell 2000 index of smaller companies was down 32.84, or 3.97 percent, at 795.18.   

The plunge in U.S. stocks caused European bourses to tumble. Britain's FTSE 100 was down 2.17 percent, Germany's DAX index fell 1.77 percent, and France's CAC-40 dropped 2.09 percent. Japan's Nikkei stock average, which closed before U.S. markets opened, rose 0.79 percent.

 HDWRAPUP 1-ECB warns of stagflation after prices spike      BYBy Henrique Almeida and Emma Davis      WC822 words   PD31 October 2007   ET18:49   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LP(Wraps ECB's Constancio, Quaden, Draghi, Weber, Bank of Spain and poll)   

LISBON/BRUSSELS, Oct 31 (Reuters) - Higher oil costs are putting Europe at risk of stagnant growth and rising prices, ECB Governing Council member Vitor Constancio said on Wednesday as euro zone inflation spiked to its highest since September 2005.   
   TDOther ECB officials also warned of slowing growth and inflation dangers, as the ECB tries to assess the impact of months of credit market turbulence and rising energy costs in the run-up to its Nov. 8 interest rate decision.   

But Belgian central bank chief Guy Quaden struck a relatively bullish note, saying the latest data supported a favourable growth outlook and that the ECB would be ready to counter inflation pressure as soon as market turmoil fades.   

Markets are trying to guess whether the ECB's tightening cycle, which took interest rates to the current 4.0 percent from 2.0 percent in 2005, has ended as the euro zone economy slows amid more expensive credit, oil and the euro currency.   

Economists polled by Reuters this week expect rates to stay on hold through 2008 [ECB/INT], though the bigger-than-expected jump in euro zone inflation to 2.6 percent in October puts extra pressure on the ECB to raise rates to tame price growth.   

"Today's number is negative information, although partly explained by statistical effects," Constancio told reporters after testifying to the Portuguese parliament.   

"2.6 percent is a very high number. We will have to analyse it. There is no pre-commitment on monetary policy," he said.   

Earlier Constancio had told lawmakers of the baleful effects of higher oil prices, hours before North Sea crude hit a fresh high above $90 a barrel <LCOc1>.   

"The price of oil is another problem that could create stagflation conditions," he said.   

The pace of the U.S. economic slowdown and how fast the U.S. dollar moves against the euro <EUR=> are other important risk factors for the world and European economy, Constancio said.   

The dollar weakened to a record $1.4472 against the euro on Wednesday, as traders expected the U.S. Federal Reserve to cut interest rates. A stronger euro mutes the effect of higher oil prices, but also makes euro-zone exports more expensive abroad.   

"The ECB is clearly facing a massive juxtaposition on rates,"  Bear Stearns economist David Brown wrote to clients.   

"Rising euro zone inflation suggests the need for higher rates, while plummeting economic confidence highlights the need for lower rates ahead. This effectively leaves policy at an impasse."   

SHARED CONCERNS   

The Bank of Spain took a downbeat view on growth in its monthly report.   

"The slowdown in 2008 euro zone economic growth will probably be somewhat sharper than expected a few months ago," it said. "In the medium term, prospects for growth have moderated as a consequence of the change in the economic and financial environment."   

ECB staff projections published in September -- when euro zone market turbulence had only been under way for a few weeks -- forecast growth to slow slightly to 2.3 percent in 2008 from an estimated 2.5 percent in 2007. Inflation was seen at 2.0 percent, just above the ECB's target for price growth.   

Italian central bank governor Mario Draghi was also cautious, saying he expected the world economy to be hit by tighter bank lending standards after the U.S. subprime mortgage crisis, though the effect so far had been limited.   

Belgium's Quaden was more optimistic, though he accepted uncertainty had increased.   

"The latest news from Europe is not bad. 2006 was an excellent year and prospects for this year and next year remain positive," he said.   

He also said that the ECB was ready to act to tame inflation if money market turbulence faded and the economy grew as expected.   

"Downside risks are ... relevant both for the growth and the inflation outlook, as they have the potential to alleviate some of the expected upward pressure on prices of a cyclical nature embedded in the baseline scenario.   

"Conversely, should the financial turbulence fade away and the main scenario be confirmed, our monetary policy should be and would be ready to counter possible upside risks to price stability," he told a business dinner in Dubai.   

This echoed the view of Bundesbank President Axel Weber in an interview with the Wall Street Journal Europe.   

"Risks to price stability have increased," he said in remarks published on Wednesday. "We at this stage cannot exclude the option that ... this will warrant further action." (Additional reporting by Sergio Goncalves in Lisbon, Andrew Hay in Madrid, Paolo Biondi in Rome, Jan Strupczewski in Brussels, London and Bangalore polling teams and Andreas Framke, Paul Carrel and David Milliken in Frankfurt)

 HDFed cuts key U.S.  interest rate  by 1/4 point      WC130 words   PD31 October 2007   ET19:15   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LPWASHINGTON, Oct 31 (Reuters) - The U.S. Federal Reserve cut the benchmark federal funds rate rate by a quarter-percentage point to 4.5 percent on Wednesday to buffer the economy against a housing downturn and tighter credit conditions.   

The decision by the central bank's Federal Open Market Committee was widely expected by financial markets. The U.S. central bank lowered rates by a more aggressive half-percentage point at a meeting last month in response to market turmoil and abruptly higher risks to economic growth.

 HDUPDATE 2-PIMCO's Gross: Further Fed cuts needed for growth      WC279 words   PD31 October 2007   ET19:53   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LP(Adds comment on non-dollar assets)   

NEW YORK, Oct 31 (Reuters) - The Federal Reserve will have to cut its federal funds target rate to between 3 and 3.5 percent over about the next year to boost U.S. economic growth, Bill Gross, manager of the world's biggest bond fund, said on Wednesday.   
   TDGross, chief investment officer of  Pacific Investment Management Co., or PIMCO, spoke on CNBC Television shortly after the Federal Open Market Committee announced it cut its target overnight rate for lending among banks by 25 basis points to 4.50 percent.   

"Ultimately, over the next six to 12 months, what the Fed has to do, and what the Fed has done in prior cycles, is to move down to a 1 percent real (as opposed to nominal) interest rate in order to restimulate the economy," Gross said.   

"Three to 3.5 percent fed funds target is where they must go," said Gross.   

He expects the U.S. economy to grow between about 1 and 2 percent over the next 12 months, inflation to run at between 2 and 2.5 percent and the jobless rate to rise above 5 percent.   

In his November Investment Outlook letter released on Monday, Gross had said that fed funds would have to go down to 3.5 percent because of "an increasingly recessionary-looking U.S. economy."   

Asked what his best investment was right now, Gross said: "Any non-dollar asset".

 HDTREASURIES-Edge lower in Asia after Fed rate cut, data eyed      BYBy Chikako Mogi      WC560 words   PD1 November 2007   ET03:16   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LPTOKYO, Nov 1 (Reuters) - U.S. Treasuries edged lower in Asia on Thursday after the Federal Reserve lowered interest rates as expected overnight but suggested it may refrain from further easing if the economy holds up.   

Treasuries fell on Wednesday after the Fed cut the federal funds rate by a quarter percentage point to 4.5 percent, and said the move "should help forestall" any further deterioration in economic growth.   
   TDThe Fed said in a statement after the policy meeting that "the upside risks to inflation roughly balance the downside risks to growth," and that it will act as needed to foster price stability and sustainable economic growth.   

"The statement was slightly more hawkish than what the market had expected, suggesting that by emphasising both the upside and the downside risks, the Fed wants to avoid the market factoring in successive rate cuts," said a dealer at a Japanese trust bank.   

"The Fed wants the market to think the next policy action will depend on data and not market expectations."   

The dealer said investors may return to Treasuries, as many players remain wary of the credit market woes.   

A Reuters survey taken shortly after the Fed rate cut found that many primary dealers think the current easing cycle has ended or will end with one more quarter-point easing.   

Twelve of the 20 primary dealers polled expect the Fed to stand pat at its next policy meeting in December, compared with 10 out of 18 dealers in a previous poll. [FED/R]   

Short-term interest rate futures were implying around a 40 percent chance the Fed will lower rates by 25 basis points again in December, to 4.25 percent, down from roughly 60 percent before the Fed's rate cut on Wednesday.   

Benchmark 10-year yields <US10YT=RR> were at 4.484 percent, inching up from 4.467 percent in late U.S. trade on Wednesday.   

Two-year Treasury notes <US2YT=RR> yielded 3.967 percent, a tad above 3.941 percent in late U.S. trade on Wednesday, and off a two-year low near 3.70 percent hit last week.   

The spread between two- and 10-year yields stood at 52 basis points, narrowing from 57 basis points which was near its widest in 2- years.   

December T-note futures <TYv1> fell 4/32 to 109-28.5/32.   

Traders were waiting for manufacturing figures due later in the session, to be followed by Friday's monthly jobs data.   

The Institute for Supply Management releases its October manufacturing index at 1400 GMT, with economists expecting a reading of 51.5 against 52.0 in September.   

For Friday's jobs data, economists expect 80,000 jobs were added in October, down from September's 110,000 gain.   

The government's initial reading on third-quarter gross domestic product growth, released on Wednesday, was an annualised 3.9 percent, its strongest quarterly growth since the first quarter of 2006. For details see [ID:nN31336431].   

The ADP National Employment Report on Wednesday showed U.S. private employers added 106,000 jobs in October, raising the prospects that Friday's payrolls will be stronger than forecast.

 HDUPDATE 3-Gulf moves to deter revaluation bets after Fed cut      BYBy Daliah Merzaban      WC781 words   PD1 November 2007   ET06:06   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LP(Updates with Qatar cuts, reserve requirement)   

DUBAI, Nov 1 (Reuters) - Saudi Arabia and other Gulf oil producers followed a U.S. interest rate cut by lowering some borrowing costs on Thursday to try to relieve pressure on their dollar-pegged currencies without stoking inflation at home.   
   TDThe Saudi riyal <SAR=> led a retreat among Gulf currencies after the rate cuts made bets on exchange-rate appreciation less attractive, and signals from the Federal Reserve diminished expectations for cheaper money in the United States.   

"If this does prove to be the end of the loosening cycle, that would be welcome by Gulf policymakers," said Simon Williams,  HSBC's regional economist in Dubai.   

"But rates are still low in nominal and real terms at a time when they should have been rising," he said.   

Most of the central bank moves reflected concerns about inflation, which is at decade highs across the Gulf, where economies are booming on a quadrupling of oil prices since 2002.   

Of the five central banks that changed rates on Thursday, only Bahrain matched Wednesday's quarter percentage point Fed easing with its benchmark rate.   

Kuwait kept its benchmark steady as did Saudi Arabia, which also tightened bank lending curbs. Qatar left its main policy signal unchanged and the United Arab Emirates reduced rates by as much as 20 basis points.   

"They are doing the minimum that they have to because of the pegs," said Marios Maratheftis, Standard Chartered's regional head of research.   

Most Gulf currencies eased and the Saudi riyal <SAR=> hit a three-week low after the central bank of the world's largest oil exporter cut its reverse repo rate by 25 basis points.   

The riyal had hit a 21-year high after the Saudi central bank opted to ignore the last Fed cut on Sept. 18, firing market speculation of an imminent revaluation.   

Since then the International Monetary Fund has urged Saudi Arabia and its neighbours make sure that interest rates were consistent with their policy of shackling currencies to the tumbling dollar in the run up to monetary union.   

Bids on the riyal fell as low as 3.7430 per dollar, its weakest since Oct. 8, after the Saudi rate cut. The central bank has officially kept the riyal stable at 3.75 to the dollar since June 1986, although on the market its latest 21-year peak was 3.7290 on Oct. 10.   

The Saudi central bank also raised the reserve requirement for banks to 9 percent from 7 percent, to prevent lower borrowing costs from increasing lending and fuelling inflation that hit a seven-year high of 4.4 percent in August.   

"This means that banks will have to keep more money in their vaults...," said John Sfakianakis, chief economist at SABB bank, one of the bankers who had seen the central bank statement.   

DILEMMA   

Saudi Arabia's dilemma mirrors that of central banks around the region, which could soon be under less pressure to choose between deterring currency appreciation and fighting inflation.   

A Reuters poll of primary dealers on Wednesday showed most expecting the Fed to keep rates on hold or end the easing cycle with another 25 basis point cut.   

"If there are no more Fed cuts from here on this does take some of the pressure off these central banks," said Caroline Grady, regional economist at  Deutsche Bank.

Gulf central banks usually track U.S. monetary policy to maintain the relative yield on their currencies. The Fed cut on Wednesday takes the gap between returns investors get on the Saudi riyal and dollar to its widest since 2002.   

The Saudi central bank left its benchmark repurchase rate unchanged at 5.5 percent with the U.S. federal funds rate at 4.5 percent. The average rate spread over the past 15 years has been 36 basis points, according to  Deutsche Bank.

The Sept. 18 Fed cut divided the six states preparing for monetary union as early as 2010. Oman, Bahrain and Saudi Arabia ignored that move. Qatar and the UAE cut some rates with Kuwait, which has tracked the dinar against a currency basket since May.   

Oman's central bank is closed on Thursdays. Qatar cut its the deposit facility rate and Kuwait its repurchase rate by 25 basis points each. Bahrain reduced all borrowing costs by a quarter point. The UAE, which has no benchmark, cut certificate of deposit rates by 20 basis points. (Additional reporting by Souhail Karam in Riyadh and Mohammed Abbas in Bahrain)

 HDCanada dollar dips on rate uncertainty, bonds mixed      BYBy John McCrank      WC776 words   PD30 October 2007   ET15:05   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LPTORONTO, Oct 30 (Reuters) - The Canadian dollar slipped against the U.S. dollar on Tuesday, amid uncertainty ahead of an impending interest rate decision by the U.S. Federal Reserve on Wednesday.   

Domestic bond prices were mixed in the wake of weaker-than-expected Canadian producer prices data showing a drop of 0.9 percent in September.   
   TDAt 9:34 a.m. (1334 GMT), the Canadian dollar was at US$1.0465, putting each U.S. dollar at 95.55 Canadian cents, down from Monday's close of US$1.0496, or 95.27 Canadian cents.   

The Canadian unit continued to benefit from strong commodities prices but was unable to reach its 47-year high of over US$1.05 on Monday, amid renewed U.S. dollar strength.   

The greenback's rebound was partly spurred by a report by Wall Street Journal's Fed watcher Greg Ip, who said a Fed rate cut was not a sure thing, said Camilla Sutton, currency strategist at Scotia Capital.   

Ip, who is known for reflecting the views of central bankers, all but nixes the idea of another 50-point cut to the fed funds rate, and suggests the Fed may not cut rates at all, while leaving the door open for future softening.   

The market has fully priced in a 25-basis-point cut in the fed funds rate to cushion the impact of the U.S. housing downturn. Many analysts see more cuts in the future.   

Before Ip's report, the main focus for Wednesday had been what the Fed would say in its statement following its rate decision, as a cut was seen as a slam dunk.   

But that's not the case anymore, said Sutton.   

"We have those calling for (a cut of) 50 (basis points), those calling for 25 and those calling for a Fed on hold, so it's definitely going to be an interesting Fed meeting tomorrow," she said.   

The U.S. central bank cut its key fed funds rate by 50 basis points to 4.75 percent in September, at a time when the market was divided over the size of its cut.   

A quarter-point cut this week would bring interest rates in the U.S. and Canada in sync for the first time since February 2005.   

Sutton said the Canadian dollar should continue to strengthen against its U.S. counterpart with or without a Fed cut, with U.S. crude oil prices <CLc1> lofty above $91 a barrel. Canada is a major oil producer and exporter.   

The North American currency pair could also be influenced this week by a slew of economic data, including Canadian and U.S. October employment figures.   

The robust Canadian dollar and the U.S. economic slowdown were seen as key factors behind the sharper-than-expected drop in Canadian producer prices, Statistics Canada said. Producer prices dropped 0.9 percent in September on a retreat in prices of vehicles, some metals and forestry products.   

BONDS LOWER   

Bond prices were weighed down by the weak producer prices data, but climbed on the long end shortly thereafter.   

While the initial movement in the bond prices was focused on the Canadian data, all eyes quickly shifted to Wednesday's Fed decision, said Max Clarke, economist at IDEAglobal in New York.   

"You're going to see some notable (U.S.) reaction following it in terms of the market not knowing exactly where to stand and I think you'll probably see (Canadian Government Bonds) follow suit," said Clarke.   

The overnight Canadian Libor rate <LIBOR01> dipped to 4.7000 percent from 4.7417 percent on Monday. The  Bank of Canada targets 4.50 percent for the overnight rate.   

Monday's CORRA rate <CORRA=> rose to 4.5195 percent from 4.500 percent on Friday. The  Bank of Canada publishes the rate at around 9:00 a.m.   

The two-year bond fell 2 Canadian cents to C$100.26 to yield 4.265 percent, while the 10-year bond gained 2 Canadian cents to C$97.89 to yield 4.269 percent.   

The yield spread between the two-year and 10-year bond moved to 15.5 basis points from 16.7 at the previous close.   

The 30-year bond rose 1 Canadian cent to C$110.87 to yield 4.343 percent. In the United States, the 30-year treasury yielded 4.669 percent.   

The three-month when-issued T-bill yielded 3.99 percent, unchanged from the previous close.

 HDKuwait rate cuts won't stoke inflation -NBK      WC357 words   PD30 October 2007   ET16:26   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LPDUBAI, Oct 30 (Reuters) - Gulf Arab oil producer Kuwait's move last month to track the U.S. Federal Reserve and cut one of its key interest rates would reduce rather than stoke inflationary pressures,  National Bank of Kuwait said on Tuesday.   

Kuwait, the Middle East's fourth-largest oil exporter, cut its repurchase rate by 50 basis points to 4.74 percent on Sept. 19, a day after an equivalent cut in the U.S. Fed funds rate.   
   TDA week earlier, Kuwait had cut the repo rate by 25 basis points in an move analysts said would deter speculation on dinar revaluation.   

But the central bank left the benchmark discount rate -- which is used by banks to set lending rates -- unchanged at 6.25 percent.   

"Far from providing a boost to credit growth and adding fuel to the inflationary fire, the move was in part an attempt by the central bank to dampen inflationary pressures,"  National Bank of Kuwait, the country's largest lender, said in a report.   

Alone among the Gulf Arab oil producers, Kuwait dropped its peg to the tumbling dollar in May to fight inflation near 12-year highs and lower the cost of some imports, a third of which the desert state pays for in euros.   

Banks use the repo rate to set deposit rates, thus making dinar assets less attractive to international investors, NBK said.   

"By increasing the opportunity cost to speculators of betting on a dinar revaluation" the move restricted liquidity inflows from abroad, capping money supply growth that would fuel inflation, NBK said.   

With future Fed cuts looming -- economists polled by Reuters expect the Fed will cut rates by a further 25 basis points before the end of the year -- the Kuwait central bank would likely continue with this strategy, NBK said.   

"CBK is able to track future interest rate cuts ... whilst balancing the needs of the domestic economy by keeping lending rates relatively high," NBK said.   

The basket to which Kuwait now pegs its dinar currency is comprised mainly of dollar.

 HDBrazil stocks fall on US rate doubts, real firmer      WC446 words   PD30 October 2007   ET16:39   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LP(Updates to close)   

SAO PAULO, Oct 30 (Reuters) - Brazil's stock market fell on Tuesday on concerns the U.S. Federal Reserve may not cut interest rates on Wednesday to revive the economy, while the country's currency firmed slightly on growing capital inflows.   
   TDThe Bovespa index <.BVSP> of the Sao Paulo Stock Exchange fell 1.02 percent to 64,383.13 points, falling below the 65,000-point mark after a record close of 65,044 on Monday. The index has gained about 46 percent so far this year.   

Brazil's currency, the real <BRBY>, gained 0.17 percent to 1.753 per U.S. dollar.   

A Wall Street Journal article on Tuesday cast doubt on the chances for a Fed rate cut, sending the Dow Jones industrial average lower and putting pressure on Brazilian markets.   

"The market is cautious. Overseas, there has been some profit-taking and here the market is taking its foot from the accelerator a bit as well," said Luiz Pizani, a trader at the Liquidez brokerage. "Everyone is trying to find hints on what the Fed decision will be."   

The real strengthened even after the central bank bought dollars in the foreign exchange market. The currency has benefited from continued dollar inflows, Pizani said.   

"Capital inflows continue to be very strong, from investments to the stock market and from exporters," he said.   

Interest-rate futures <0#DIJ:> on the BM&F commodities and futures exchange in Sao Paulo were mostly higher, after data released on Tuesday showed Brazil's broadest inflation measure rose more than expected in October. The IGP-M index rose 1.05 percent, compared with the 0.85 percent median forecast by 15 analysts in a Reuters survey.   

Shares in mining giant CVRD , the second most heavily weighted stock in the Bovespa index, fell 2 percent to 53.9 reais, retreating after a 4.56 percent surge the previous session, as prices of copper, zinc, nickel and other metals fell in international markets.   

State oil company  Petrobras , the top heavyweight at the Bovespa, lost 3.86 percent to 70.02 reais as oil prices fell from record highs, down more than 3 percent in London and New York as expectations grew that supplies rose last week.   

Shares of Bovespa Holding , the holding company that controls the Sao Paulo Stock Exchange, fell 2.66 percent to 31.15 reais, adding to an 8.55 percent tumble in the previous session. The stock surged 52 percent in its first trading day on Friday.

 HDFED FOCUS-No rate cut would spark question of what Fed knows      BYBy Herbert Lash      WC811 words   PD30 October 2007   ET18:17   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LPNEW YORK, Oct 30 (Reuters) - Federal Reserve policy-makers are widely expected to cut U.S. interest rates on Wednesday, but if they make no move, investors will wonder what the Fed knows that they don't and question its commitment to transparency.   

Anticipation of a rate cut drove a two-week rally in bonds until late last week, when an upbeat outlook from  Microsoft and a profit forecast from struggling mortgage lender  Countrywide Financial took some steam out of U.S. Treasury bonds.   
   TDBut stocks also have rallied -- at least in part -- on expectations the Fed will ease and the dollar has fallen to record lows in the last few weeks in anticipation of a cut.   

At the same time, oil prices hit a record high on Monday, and if the October jobs report at the end of the week shows a strong labor market, economists say a rate cut would fan inflation worries. On the other hand, some are concerned that a cut in rates would unfairly bail out investors who have been hurt by the troubles in the subprime mortgage market.   

Short-term U.S. interest rate futures on Tuesday showed a 94 percent chance the Fed will cut rates this week <FFX7> against 98 percent on Monday.   

"If the Fed does not cut interest rates our speculation will be that the Friday unemployment report will be at the very least firm and that does risk a rise in interest rates across the board," said Jane Caron, chief economic strategist at Dwight Asset Management Co in Burlington, Vermont.   

Stocks would likely immediately sell off on no Fed move and short-term bond prices would likely fall, Caron said. What longer-term bonds would do is harder to tell and would depend on the post-meeting statement.   

If the Fed leaves policy unchanged, Caron said, policy-makers are likely to say they are carefully monitoring the economy and are prepared to act. But a rate cut and suggestions of more to come would push long-term bond prices down on inflation worries, she said.   

The Fed has a "very difficult call" to make, but a cut will again raise the question of whether the Fed is taking risk out of the investment equation, Caron added. If it does not ease, "there's going to be a lot of criticism about a lack of transparency."   

ECONOMY OR MARKETS   

The Fed's mandate is the keep inflation in check and the economy growing. That makes unemployment and jobs creation key to understanding a policy decision, said John Davidson, chief executive of ParnerRe in Greenwich, Connecticut.   

"If they don't do it, I think it will be because they think the economy is strong enough, it doesn't need further cuts," Davidson said. "If they do it, they do it based on continued weakness in housing and some initial signs of some weakness in employment, associated with the initial jobless claims."   

Davidson agrees with the consensus view that the Fed will cut the fed funds rate by one-quarter of percentage point. The next likelihood would be no move at all because the Fed should not bail out investors who are imprudent, he said.   

"I do think that the Fed is there to bail out the overall economy so that the penalties that should be absorbed by those who took out too much risk do not extend beyond the risk takers," Davidson said.   

The Fed's half-point cut in September has spurred record high oil prices and pushed the dollar down -- about 3 percent -- which points against a rate cut on Wednesday, said Joseph Battipaglia, market strategist at  Stifel Nicolaus.

"Since the massive intervention by the Fed, the credit markets have been recovering, though they are not fully recovered," he said. "On the economic front we still have a 3 percent growth rate, low unemployment and a pricing environment that doesn't show a lot of slack."   

Battipaglia said that in the past 30 days "there seems to be less Fed speak and demands from Congress about what the Fed can do to stop a meltdown in the economy, which suggests they can take a much more measured look."   

The tumbling dollar and surging oil may lead policy-makers to sit tight, said John Hardy, market strategist at Denmark's Saxo Bank. But the Fed also must avoid disappointing market expectations by not cutting, he said in a research note.   

"So perhaps the highest odds scenario is that the Fed does cut, but injects firm, hawkish language that gives the Fed maximum flexibility going forward," Hardy said. (Additional reporting by Jennifer Coogan)

 HDFed meets with chances high for small rate cut      BYBy Glenn Somerville      WC567 words   PD30 October 2007   ET19:03   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LPWASHINGTON, Oct 30 (Reuters) - Federal Reserve policy-makers began meeting on Tuesday against the backdrop of a still-plummeting U.S. housing market that is sapping consumer optimism and may require more interest-rate tonic.   

The U.S. central bank's Federal Open Market Committee began a two-day meeting at 2 p.m. (1800 GMT) with futures markets betting that it will announce a quarter-percentage-point cut in rates at about 2:15 p.m. (1815 GMT) on Wednesday.   
   TDThat would be on top of a surprise half-point reduction the Fed made on Sept. 18 to its trend-setting federal funds rate for overnight loans between banks and would bring the key rate to 4.5 percent, its lowest since March 2006.   

There was a only a slight doubt in financial markets on Tuesday whether policy-makers would cut rates on Wednesday, with futures markets pricing in more than a 90 percent chance for a small reduction.   

Another dose of bad news on housing on Tuesday morning helped dissipate lingering doubts on rate cuts.   

The  Standard & Poor's/Case Shiller national home price index showed prices in 10 major metropolitan areas fell 0.8 percent in August -- a reminder of the deep housing-sector slide that policy-makers say is a key risk to the economy.   

The report showed home prices were down 5 percent from year-ago levels, the biggest year-over-year decline since June 1991, just after the 1990-91 recession ended.   

Not surprisingly, separate data on Tuesday from the Conference Board showed consumer confidence tumbled for a third straight month in October, reaching a two-year low.   

"Further weakening in business conditions has, yet again, tempered consumers' assessment of current-day conditions and may very well be a prelude to lackluster job growth in the months ahead," said Lynn Franco, director of the Conference Board's consumer research center.   

During the two-day meeting, in which the Fed may also resume a discussion on potential changes to their communications policy, officials will get a reading on third-quarter economic growth, which should at least assure them that a precipitous decline in activity has not taken hold.   

Economists surveyed by Reuters predict that gross domestic product figures on Wednesday morning will show the economy expanded at a 3 percent annual rate in the third quarter. That will be only a moderate easing from the 3.8 percent growth in the second quarter, although a steeper slowing is expected in the final three months of the year.   

The expected fourth-quarter softness puts a burden on Fed Chairman Ben Bernanke and his colleagues to meet their test of sustaining a noninflationary expansion at time when a housing downturn and credit-market strains are weighing heavily.   

In a speech on Oct. 19, Bernanke said that during times of stress, policy-makers must be prepared to counter uncertainty by acting boldly with measures to ward off a worse situation.   

"Intuition suggests that stronger action by the central bank may be warranted to prevent particularly costly outcomes," Bernanke said -- words that would echo the thoughts of many of those on Wall Street.

 HDRPT-TREASURIES-Bonds fall after Fed cuts, but hints at pause      BYBy Chris Reese      WC522 words   PD31 October 2007   ET12:59   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LP(Adds economist quote, updates prices)   

NEW YORK, Oct 31 (Reuters) - U.S. Treasury debt prices fell on Wednesday after the Federal Reserve cut benchmark interest rates as expected but signaled it may refrain from further easing if the economy holds up.   
   TDThe central bank cut the federal funds rate, the recommended overnight lending rate among banks, by a quarter percentage point to 4.50 percent, and said the move "should help forestall" any further deterioration in economic growth.   

Bonds extended losses immediately after the Fed statement.   

"(The Fed) gave the market a rate cut today with one hand, but with the other hand they pulled the rug out from under those who were looking for more rate cuts," said Chris Rupkey, senior financial economist at  Bank of Tokyo-Mitsubishi UFJ in New York.   

Benchmark 10-year notes <US10YT=RR> traded 21/32 lower in price for a yield of 4.47 percent from 4.39 percent late on Tuesday. Benchmark yields, which move inversely to prices, reached as high as 4.48 percent, the loftiest in over a week, and marking the biggest single-day jump in 10-year yields in over three weeks.   

"The market was expecting greater hints about the likelihood of further easing," said Richard Iley, senior economist at  BNP Paribas in New York.   

Short-term interest rate futures slipped on Wednesday, with futures implying a 42 percent chance the Fed will lower rates by 25 basis points again in December, to 4.25 percent, against 64 percent overnight. Bigger losses were seen in 2008 contracts as dealers scaled back ideas of rate cuts in the new year.   

Bonds had already been trading lower before the Fed statement, after stronger-than-expected jobs and economic growth data early in the day, along with stock market gains.   

The government's initial reading on third-quarter gross domestic product growth, released on Wednesday morning, was an annualized 3.9 percent, its strongest quarterly growth since the first quarter of 2006. For details see [ID:nN31336431].   

Earlier, the ADP National Employment Report showed U.S. private employers added 106,000 jobs in October, raising the prospects that the government's payrolls data on Friday will be stronger than the consensus forecast, analysts said.   

Economists expect 80,000 jobs were added to U.S. nonfarm payrolls in October, down from September's 110,000 gain, a recent Reuters poll showed.   

Two-year Treasury notes <US2YT=RR> traded 9/32 lower in price for a yield of 3.95 percent from 3.81 percent late on Tuesday. While two-year notes fell in price on Wednesday, their yields in October posted the fifth monthly drop in a row, which was their longest winning streak in four years.   

Five-year notes <US5YT=RR> traded 16/32 lower for a yield of 4.17 percent from 4.06 percent, while the 30-year bond <US30YT=RR> traded 1-2/32 lower in price for a yield of 4.75 percent.

 HD3-month euro Libor rates fixed higher, dollar rates fall      WC298 words   PD31 October 2007   ET13:00   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LPLONDON, Oct 31 (Reuters) - London interbank lending rates for three-month euro deposits fixed slightly higher on Wednesday for the third straight session, while dollar rates fell ahead of an expected interest rate cut from the Federal Reserve.   

The rise in euro rates marks the first time in two months that three-month Libors have been fixed higher for three consecutive days, according to the daily fixing data by the British Bankers Association.   
   TDThe BBA fixings also showed that three-month dollar Libor rates fell to their lowest since March last year and were fixed lower for the 17th straight session.   

Three-month euro rates <EUR3MFSR=> rose to 4.60313 percent from 4.60250 percent on Tuesday, having hit their lowest level in over two months last Friday.   

Two-month euro Libor rates <EUR2MFSR=>, which now cover the year-end period, were at 4.58563 percent, slightly lower from Tuesday's near 30 basis point surge to 4.58750 percent.   

Three-month sterling rates <GBP3MFSR=> were fixed at 6.27938 percent from Tuesday's 6.27050 percent.   

Libor rates for three-month dollar deposits <USD3MFSR=> fell to 4.89375 percent, their lowest since March 2006, from 4.91125 percent on Tuesday, the BBA data showed.   

Dollar rates are coming down as investors anticipate the Fed will cut benchmark interest rates to 4.5 percent on Wednesday, although they're trimming their bets on a follow-up cut in December.   

Three-month rates, particularly in euro and sterling deposits, had shot up in August and September as banks hoarded cash as contingency to cover losses in their structured products hit by the credit crisis.

 HDUS RATE FUTURES-Q3 growth casts doubt on Fed decision      BYBy Ros Krasny      WC327 words   PD31 October 2007   ET13:39   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LP(Adds details, analyst comments)   

CHICAGO, Oct 31 (Reuters) - A stronger-than-expected reading on U.S. third-quarter economic growth has cast doubt on Federal Reserve monetary policy, hours before the Fed announces its latest decision on benchmark interest rates.   
   TDShort-term rate futures, which measure market expectations on Fed policy, slipped after Commerce Department data showed third-quarter growth at its strongest since the first quarter of 2006.   

Implied prospects for the Fed to lower interest rates today <FFX7> fell as low as 86 percent from 94 percent on Tuesday, but quickly rebounded to 90 percent.   

Bigger losses were logged in futures contracts for 2008 delivery, suggesting the market is anticipating less Fed policy easing in the new year.   

U.S. advance third-quarter gross domestic product rose by a 3.9 percent annual rate, up from 3.8 percent in the second quarter and well above the consensus forecast of 3.0 percent.   

With growth above trend, the case for follow-up interest rate cuts by the Federal Open Market Committee to its one-half-percentage point September ease looks less persuasive.   

"The Fed will have to mention the strong growth in their statement," said David Sloan, economist at 4CAST Ltd in New York.   

Still, analysts said policy-makers will probably be more concerned with fresh signs of weakness in the housing market along with declining consumer confidence that threatens to infect spending patterns in the months ahead.   

Many economists forecast much lower growth in the fourth quarter and in early 2008.   

"The big question is how the economy performs in Q4 and how much spillover there is from dire residential investment. This data does very little to resolve the question," said Alan Ruskin, chief international strategist at RBS Greenwich Capital in Greenwich, Connecticut.

 HDFed rate cut this week not a sure thing -WSJ      WC365 words   PD30 October 2007   ET02:56   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LPTOKYO, Oct 30 (Reuters) - A Federal Reserve interest rate cut this week is no sure thing and officials are not seriously considering a half-point reduction in overnight rates, the Wall Street Journal reported on Tuesday without citing sources.   

The article by Greg Ip, the Journal's Fed watcher who is known for sometimes reflecting the views of senior central bankers, said policymakers view this week's decision as a choice between a quarter-point cut to 4.5 percent and not moving at all.   
   TDInvestors have widely expected the Fed to cut rates at a two-day meeting ending on Wednesday, following a half-point slash in September, to limit the economic damage from the housing market's incessant slide.   

Futures on the fed funds rate have shown a small chance of a half-point cut.   

Currency traders in Tokyo said the article helped nudge the dollar up slightly from near record lows against the euro and multi-decade lows against other major currencies.   

Ip said perhaps the biggest risk for the Fed is that the market's certainty on a pending rate cut puts a burden on the central bank to deliver.   

"But the current market environment is more fragile than usual, and thus the consequences of disappointing the market are potentially more damaging. Against that, the Fed will have to weigh the risk that a cut will stoke inflationary psychology," Ip wrote in the article on the Journal's Web site,   www.wsj.com  .   

The Fed can mitigate such risks with its post-meeting statement by either leaving the door open to a future cut if it does not move this week or by dampening expectations for future monetary easing if it does lower rates, Ip said.   

Ip said the case for keeping policy on hold comes down to the economic outlook.   

While the housing market has deteriorated further, there has been little evidence of spillover into the broader economy and Fed officials "don't appear to have significantly altered their forecast of a return to moderate growth next year," Ip said.

 HDASSET-BACKEDS-ABX up post-Fed, Sallie Mae deal eyed      BYBy Nancy Leinfuss      WC490 words   PD31 October 2007   ET21:51   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LP(Updates to add quotes)   

NEW YORK, Oct 31 (Reuters) - A key derivatives index tied to subprime mortgages bounced back above record lows on Wednesday as the Federal Reserve unleashed its second round of interest-rate cuts in two months to ease credit conditions.   
   TD"The Fed's Halloween cut turned out to be neither a trick nor a treat, with 25 basis points coming in as expected - not as good as an XXL (extra, extra large) Snickers bar, but better than an old box of raisins," one dealer said.   

The Fed cut the key federal funds and discount rates by a quarter-percentage point each on Wednesday. The latest action follows a half-percentage point rate cut last month by the central bank.   

The top-rated slices of the ABX were driven 3 to 5 points higher on short-covering ahead of the Fed's key announcement on Wednesday, but later gave back some of the gains after the latest rate cut was deemed not enough.   

"This morning was kind of quiet with indexes trading around the low, but then we saw a rally right before the Fed," one ABX trader said. "People began buying 'AAA' and 'AA' indexes and at one point, they were up by as much as 5 points."   

The top "AAA" slice of the benchmark ABX 07-1 index shot up by several points on Wednesday to 82.72, versus a previous record low close of 79.28, while the "AA" tier climbed to 49.57, versus a 45.72 record low close on Tuesday, traders said.   

"After the announcement, the index came back down to earth somewhat, with increased selling interest from shorts and profit-takers balancing out the buying flows," the dealer said. "There were very good flows over the session as the index finished broadly positive to break its recent downtrend."   

The riskiest "BBB-" slice of the ABX 07-1 index traded up to 18.94 on Wednesday from 17.36 at the prior close, traders said. The index has tumbled by 80 percent this year as the subprime mortgage crisis intensified.   

The index used by investors to hedge subprime mortgage exposure tumbled to record lows over recent days after October subprime loan performance data revealed delinquencies on loans made to risky borrowers had increased further.   

Credit rating agencies Moody's Investors Service and  Standard & Poor's each downgraded billions of dollars worth of subprime mortgage securities over recent weeks.   

In the primary sector, Sallie Mae will lead issuance in the market this week with a $2.0 billion student loan ABS offering, which is expected to meet with good demand.   

The deal is currently being marketd to investors by underwriters  Barclays Capital,  Credit Suisse,  Lehman Brothers, RBS Greenwich Capital and  Wachovia Securites, dealers said.

 HDTREASURIES-Bonds rise on weaker stocks, writedown fears      WC279 words   PD1 November 2007   ET12:57   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LP(Updates market action, adds jobless claims data)   

NEW YORK, Nov 1 (Reuters) - U.S. Treasury debt prices rose on Thursday, as safe-haven demand emerged on an expected weaker opening for the stock market due to disappointing earnings and worries about more bank writedowns.   
   TDAlso, government data showing tame inflation also bolstered bond prices, a day after the Federal Open Market Committee invoked inflation concerns in its monetary policy statement.   

Treasuries slipped in overnight trading as traders trimmed bets for future interest rate cuts by the Federal Reserve after it raised doubts whether it would cut benchmark rates further.   

Bond bulls argued further deterioration in the financial sector stemming from the housing slump and credit turmoil would pressure policy-makers to lower rates more in coming months.   

Worries about the financial sector intensified on Thursday after  Credit Suisse reported a $1.9 billion writedown on bad loans and mortgage investments and brokerage downgrades of  Citigroup due to capital concerns.   

These reports suggest  Citigroup, the biggest U.S. bank, "is under-capitalized and won't be able to deal with the blow from the consumer. This is helping Treasuries," said T.J. Marta, fixed income strategist with  RBC Capital Markets in New York.   

The price on benchmark 10-year debt <US10YT=RR> was up 11/32, wiping out an earlier 10/32 decline. The 10-year yield was 4.43 percent, down from 4.47 percent late Wednesday but up as high as 4.51 percent in earlier trading.

 HD3-month euro Libor rates fixed higher for 2nd day      WC289 words   PD30 October 2007   ET13:02   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LPLONDON, Oct 30 (Reuters) - London interbank lending rates for three-month euro and sterling deposits rose on Tuesday, while dollar rates fell ahead of Wednesday's expected interest rate cut from the Federal Reserve.   

The rise in euro rates marks the first time in almost a month three-month Libors have been fixed higher two days in a row, according to the daily fixing data by the British Bankers Association.   
   TDThe BBA fixings also showed that three-month sterling Libors marked their biggest jump in two weeks, while dollar rates fell to their lowest since March last year.   

Three-month euro rates <EUR3MFSR=> rose to 4.60250 percent from 4.60063 percent on Monday, having hit their lowest level in over two months on Friday.   

Three-month sterling rates <GBP3MFSR=> were fixed at 6.27500 percent from Monday's 2-1/2 week low of 6.26750 percent.   

Libor rates for three-month dollar deposits <USD3MFSR=> fell to 4.91125 percent, their lowest since March 2006, from 4.96 percent, the BBA data showed.   

Dollar rates are coming down as investors anticipate the Fed will cut benchmark interest rates to 4.5 percent on Wednesday, although they're trimming their bets on a follow-up cut in December.   

Three-month rates, particularly in euro and sterling deposits, had shot up in August and September as banks hoarded cash as contingency to cover losses in their structured products hit by the credit crisis. Expectations for steady or lower interest rates and measures by central banks to calm money markets have pulled rates off these peaks.

 HDUPDATE 1-COMMODITIES-Markets down ahead of Fed rate move      BYBy Barani Krishnan and Veronica Brown      WC556 words   PD30 October 2007   ET13:29   SNReuters News   SCLBA   LAEnglish   CY(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   
   LP(Recasts, updates with U.S. markets' activity, adds NEW YORK to dateline)   

NEW YORK/LONDON, Oct 30 (Reuters) - Energy, metals and agricultural markets were down broadly on Tuesday as investors took profit from recent highs before a critical meeting Wednesday on U.S. interest rates.   
   TDIf the Federal Reserve cuts rates at the end of the meeting to avoid an economic slowdown, like it did in September, the dollar will get hammered again and that could create inflationary pressures that push oil up to $100 a barrel and gold $800 an ounce, analysts said.   

But if the Fed leaves rates where they are, the dollar could rebound sharply from the record lows it has struck against the euro for weeks now, resulting in an abrupt devaluation of commodities.   

"Everyone's looking to the Fed to cut rates by a quarter point, and if they do that, all those commodities priced in the dollar are likely to have a nice little jolt to the upside," Adam Sarhan, a Florida-based analyst at GlobalMacroResearch.com, said.   

"But if Fed remains flat, it will catch a lot of people off-guard," he added.   

The dollar sank to a new all-time low against the euro on Tuesday, with futures markets betting that the Fed's key rate will fall to 4.5 percent after Wednesday's meeting from the current 4.75 percent. Before September's cut, the rate was 5.25 percent.   

U.S. crude oil futures settled down $3.15 at $90.38 a barrel after hitting a record high of $93.80 in the previous session. London Brent fell $2.88 to $87.44, down from Monday's peak of $90.49.   

Interest rate fears aside, profit-taking in oil was encouraged by an expected recovery to Mexican oil exports, which have been disrupted since last week by foul weather.   

Adding to the bearish sentiment, traders said, were forecasts that a government report to be released Wednesday would show an increase in U.S. crude stocks. S]   

Most-active gold futures for December delivery on the COMEX division of the New York Mercantile Exchange settled down $4.80 at $787.80 an ounce.   

Spot prices for gold bullion fell to $781.25/781.85 an ounce in late afternoon trade in New York, against Monday's comparative level of $788.90/789.70. Bullion had hit $794.40 in the last 24 hours, its highest since January 1980 when prices rose to a record high of $850.   

In copper, COMEX's December contract ended down 3.95 cents at $3.4815 a lb. Copper for delivery in three months on the London Metal Exchange (LME) last traded at $7,710.50 a tonne, down $134.50 from Monday's close.   

Leading agricultural commodities on the Chicago Board of Trade tumbled across the board.   

CBOT wheat for December closed down 14-1/2 cents at $8.14 per bushel, after hitting limit-up on Monday.   

Corn for December settled down 5-3/4 cents at $3.70-1/4 per bushel.   

November soybeans ended down 19 cents at $9.92 per bushel.
